<div id="review_800158367" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/800158367" />
    <a title="Ingrid Hall" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16107197-ingrid-hall"><img alt="Ingrid Hall" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442895363p2/16107197.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/800158367?book_show_action=true">Dec 26, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ingrid Hall" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ingrid Hall" href="/user/show/16107197-ingrid-hall">Ingrid Hall</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer800158367" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8123977530940220920">I had very high hopes about Sex in the Title a comedy revolving around the lives of several young men and it's fair to say that the first few chapters certainly didn't disappoint! I thought the parody of Sex in the City was clever and loved that the book is told purely from the male perspective all the way throughout and the character's, their experiences and the way they see things definitely had more than a ring of truth about it.<br/><br/>Evan as a character totally hooked me and I was practically wett</span>
  <span id="freeText8123977530940220920" style="display:none">I had very high hopes about Sex in the Title a comedy revolving around the lives of several young men and it's fair to say that the first few chapters certainly didn't disappoint! I thought the parody of Sex in the City was clever and loved that the book is told purely from the male perspective all the way throughout and the character's, their experiences and the way they see things definitely had more than a ring of truth about it.<br /><br />Evan as a character totally hooked me and I was practically wetting myself with laughter by the time we got to the scene where the prostitute took a nice big bite out of his...well, you get the picture! The prostitute(s), I have to say were also scarily convincing and I thought that the author captured their voice and spirit exceptionally well.<br /><br />Now I get to the but...and for me the major failing of this book. The author chooses this point, when we are totally sucked up into Evan's world (pardon my dreadful pun) to switch viewpoint to another male character and so starts the frenetic head hopping...as character after character is thrown at us and we are invited into their heads/their worlds. There is also a distinct lack of sex in the book. I stopped reading the book for over a week after the author moved away from Evan and forced myself to return to it because I could see that the book had potential. The next few chapters bored the life out me and then, just when I had totally become sold on Carlos and in particular his wonderfully written relationship with Carolina the author did it again and flicked viewpoint...<br /><br />Evan and Carlos are for me the two stand out characters of this book. The rest of the characters I could take or leave, preferably leave and I think the author has missed a golden opportunity with this book because had he chosen to focus purely on those two, alternating possibly chapter by chapter between them then I think he could have had a best seller. However, in flicking viewpoint between so many male heads he is in danger of losing his readership...he certainly lost me at several points.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8123977530940220920" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7007136727315489086"><b>***3.5 Funny Stars***</b><br/><br/>I first came across this author on FB, he was hosting a thread on one of my favorite blogs and he was totally hilarious and charming, all the girls and myself included were having a great time interacting with this guy, immediately I decided to get a copy of <i> Sex in the Title</i> and started reading.<br/><br/>What is interesting about this book is that, is not only written by a man, but that it's about the dating experiences men go through and those can messy and yet fascinating.   <span id="freeText7007136727315489086" style="display:none"><b>***3.5 Funny Stars***</b><br><br>I first came across this author on FB, he was hosting a thread on one of my favorite blogs and he was totally hilarious and charming, all the girls and myself included were having a great time interacting with this guy, immediately I decided to get a copy of <i> Sex in the Title</i> and started reading.<br><br>What is interesting about this book is that, is not only written by a man, but that it's about the dating experiences men go through and those can messy and yet fascinating. This book is set in New York City and it follows the lives of five completely different guys, sort of like a male version of Sex in the City.<br><br>Zack Love's writing style is very smart and sophisticated and I personally loved that, I must say though that I'd frequently had to interrupt my reading to Google a lot of the big words he used. I found the dialogues a lot more interesting than the actual plot, a lot of the situations this guys found themselves in seemed very unrealistic to me. All of this men had different characteristics but not one of them I found interesting or attractive in any way, which is the reason why I found myself getting a little bored from time to time.<br><br> <a href="http://s1366.photobucket.com/user/DVFmontoya/media/399e9db6-bfed-4caf-a300-7d2ec52f6178_zpsc45c2d93.png.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

</a><br><br><br>Overall reading this book was a good experience, there were some seriously funny scenes that had me laughing and ultimately it was really interesting to read a book from the male perspective which once again brought me to the conclusion that women are from Venus and men are from Mars... </span>

<div id="review_780620567" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/780620567" />
    <a title="Paul Little" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17864015-paul-little"><img alt="Paul Little" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1365762428p2/17864015.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/780620567?book_show_action=true">Dec 04, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paul Little" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paul Little" href="/user/show/17864015-paul-little">Paul Little</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer780620567" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11640942104615998053">This is a rather funny book that has so far been very well received since its release. It is worth this praise and success in large measure because it is a witty, well thought out, splendidly executed satire on growing up at the time when I grew up. It is certainly funny in of itself, but now it also has that sort of ‘retro’ feel to it, that half emotional ambience about how things were so much better / downright archaic back at the turn of the century (depending upon whether you grew up then or</span>
  <span id="freeText11640942104615998053" style="display:none">This is a rather funny book that has so far been very well received since its release. It is worth this praise and success in large measure because it is a witty, well thought out, splendidly executed satire on growing up at the time when I grew up. It is certainly funny in of itself, but now it also has that sort of ‘retro’ feel to it, that half emotional ambience about how things were so much better / downright archaic back at the turn of the century (depending upon whether you grew up then or after).<br /> The book does cover the evergreen issue of coming to terms with life and finding a niche within it that fits somewhere between the ambitions we set ourselves as youngsters and the realities of the daily grind. There are very few people who have it easy all of the time and that extends into all aspects of life. Contrary to the title’s clever marketing, this is not all about sex, but in the way that American Pie was not all about sex, because you can clearly argue that it is, even though the bonding of friends who hold firm intially opposing and then embracing the inevitable pressures of growing up is very important to the story.<br /> It is a very important positive that the author does not stray away from the comic into the embarrassing which is all too easy pitfall. It was to me a tale of coincidence and growing up, a story about how to deal with life when all life is sending is hard knocks; it is also a little bit of a heart warmer because it does help us recall that, more often than not, it does work out, even though nothing like originallt intentioned.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11640942104615998053" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

This book is not from my usual genre so I wasn’t sure how I would go reading it, but it ended up being a page turner and extremely well written from a male perspective.<br/><br/>During this fantastic adventure we meet five men, Evan, Sammy (Heeb), Carlos, Trevor and Yi Wang (Narc) as we wander through their dating disasters.   <span id="freeText16008717242119008425" style="display:none">Reviewer: Kaylene - Magic Within The Pages<br />Rating: 5 Stars<br /><br />Sex in the Title is a lovely surprise and very, very funny. This book is not from my usual genre so I wasn’t sure how I would go reading it, but it ended up being a page turner and extremely well written from a male perspective.<br /><br />During this fantastic adventure we meet five men, Evan, Sammy (Heeb), Carlos, Trevor and Yi Wang (Narc) as we wander through their dating disasters. It is really interesting reading a male perspective on dating and their misadventures and/or successes.<br /><br />This book is clever, whity, smart, edited to perfection, but most importantly it is well constructed with extremely well developed characters and individual stories.<br /><br />I am so pleased I found this little gem, well actually it was recommended to me so I am now going to recommend it to you . This is a debut novel from Zach Love and I highly recommend it as a fantastic read and one not to be missed. Get your fingers one-clicking this one today. <br /><br />This book was purchased and reviewed by Kaylene for Magic Within the Pages. </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anna- Maria Butucescu" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anna- Maria Butucescu" href="/user/show/12609784-anna--maria-butucescu">Anna- Maria Butucescu</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer819957832" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13319896189390932823">"I don't know the question, but sex is definitely the answer"- Woody Allen used to say - and clearly this resonates in Zack Love's title. But, contrary to the salacious introduction, this book isn' t just about sex.<br/> Following the (mis)adventures of five ethnically diverse young men in their pursuit of sex, love and ultimately happiness, Sex in the Title is a piercing satire drawing inspiration from love, friendship and the challenges of adulthood. The obstacles life throws our way and the coping</span>
  <span id="freeText13319896189390932823" style="display:none">"I don't know the question, but sex is definitely the answer"- Woody Allen used to say - and clearly this resonates in Zack Love's title. But, contrary to the salacious introduction, this book isn' t just about sex.<br /> Following the (mis)adventures of five ethnically diverse young men in their pursuit of sex, love and ultimately happiness, Sex in the Title is a piercing satire drawing inspiration from love, friendship and the challenges of adulthood. The obstacles life throws our way and the coping mechanisms we develop, the gap between unrealistic youthful ambitions, the goals we set ourselves and the choices we ultimately make, the adult-sized dramas no one has prepared us for, but which we suddenly find ourselves confronted with are all, in and of themselves, a rich source of humour.<br /> The story is not only witty and downright hilarious, but intricately thought out and the reader will be immersed in its entertaining twists and turns from the very first pages.<br /> Zach Love's debut singles him out as a talent to watch. Read his novel, there will be more to come!</span>
  <a data-text-id="13319896189390932823" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground">Readers also enjoyed</h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent"><div class='bookCarousel'>
<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_53158917'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/53158917-double-trouble"><img alt="Double Trouble" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1586772023l/53158917._SX98_.jpg" />
</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('9wu2VR5/PXw65+OlXa3yf+2V6v5IW3pBlxWCuVQIDc/fPm04wQsbMBmzKvCV0XBUcPdW0Hi/FUXyl4sfr47Ibw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('PSyn2Hab3N+zgY9q1FJxhef2G5SrsR3coNJaHFcgQvUVGXy1qe/6k5DVRj8cLvOuepSnuptVctjFUFO6rKaHVQ==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<span id="freeTextContainer17287055729612455600">Pardon the minimal content here. You're more likely to find new stuff on my author site: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://zacklove.com'>http://zacklove.com</a><br/><br/>And here's my bio:<br/><br/>Zack Love graduated from Harvard College, where he studied mostly literature, psychology, philosophy, and film. After college, he moved to New York City and took a corporate consulting job that had absolutely nothing to do with his studies. The attacks of September 11, 2001</span>
  <span id="freeText17287055729612455600" style="display:none">Pardon the minimal content here. You're more likely to find new stuff on my author site: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://zacklove.com">http://zacklove.com</a><br /><br />And here's my bio:<br /><br />Zack Love graduated from Harvard College, where he studied mostly literature, psychology, philosophy, and film. After college, he moved to New York City and took a corporate consulting job that had absolutely nothing to do with his studies. The attacks of September 11, 2001 inspired him to write a novelette titled “The Doorman" (<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://tinyurl.com/TheDoormanAmazon">http://tinyurl.com/TheDoormanAmazon</a>), and heightened his interest in the Middle East. A decade later, that interest extended to the Syrian Civil war, which provided the backdrop for his latest work. In late 2013, Zack began releasing his unpublished works of fiction and became a full-time author. He has published comedy, psychological and philosophical fiction, and romance. Zack enjoys confining himself to one genre about as much as he likes trying to sum up his existence in one paragraph.</span>

            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Every human relationship begins with a coincidence. Even the most fundamental relationship - that of parent and child - begins entirely with a coincidence. The child is produced by whatever serendipity brought its parents together, and the fact that the child was born to its particular parents instead of to another couple is pure happenstance. Thus, children have no choice over the relationship that is most important to their existence.<br />By contrast, friends and lovers choose each other, but even these choices are reactions to whatever random coincidence made the resulting relationship possible.&rdquo;</span>
